## Page 324

RevOps
•Automated reporting.
•Predictive forecasting across GT M .
•CRM  health and hygiene.
•Automation creation.
•M onitoring of CRM .
•AI-driven enablement through mock calls and meetings.
•Company-wide knowledge base.
ese use cases are just scratching the surface. W hat they all have in
common is that you can do more with less. is creates massive productivity
gains.
“AI will not replace RevOps—i t w ill amplify it. e real impact of AI in
RevOps is automation at scale, enabling teams to focus on strategy rather than
manual execution. At Blink Ops, w e’ve leveraged AI to automate lead scoring,
sales forecasting, and customer health tracking, giving our teams real-time
intelligence instead of static reports. e companies that embrace AI in RevOps
today will be the ones setting the standard for revenue operations tomorrow.”
— Leore Spira, D irector of RevOps, Blink Ops
Cost Reductions
M ost companies will adopt AI for cost reduction reasons. Less people can do
more with the use of AI. e adoption of AI requires less labor to reach the
same, even higher productivity levels.
e M cKinsey AI report states that a third of responses named cost
reduction the top reason to adopt AI.
Revenue Increases

---

## Page 325

Improvements in productivity also lead to revenue increases. For the same
reason as before, the same amount of people will be able to do more. A
business can reach more prospects, qualify leads more accurately, and
understand data better to identify juicy opportunities across the whole G T M
funnel.
Proﬁts
Increased productivity, reduced costs, and more revenue will increase proﬁts.
M cKinsey estimated that AI will add anywhere from $2.6 trillion to $4.4
trillion in global corporate proﬁts annually.42 at’s an amount in the range of
the total G D P of France and G ermany. It’s no surprise that every executive,
investor and business wants AI.
Securing the Future: Safety and AI
Security is another concern for businesses.
A notable example of this was the leak of Samsung’s IP through ChatG PT.
One employee entered conﬁdential information into ChatG PT, and that data
was used to train their model. e Samsung IP was used to provide an answer
to another ChatG PT  user, leading to the lead. As a consequence, Samsung
banned the use of ChatG PT.43
Since then, security has improved, and many generative AI tools allow for a
private model. Still, one in four businesses restricts the use of G enerative AI
tools.44 Security will continue to be a major concern for enterprises that have a
vast lake of sensitive data.
It can also reach political levels and touch upon corporate espionage. e
country where an AI system is hosted aﬀects which government may have legal
access to the data. Companies need to take these factors into account when
choosing AI services or integrating AI into their own products.
However, it’s evident that security concerns will be resolved over time.
Nothing will stop the AI revolution. For RevOps teams, it will be a question of

---

## Page 326

which AI tools and when to deploy them. For that, a good understanding of
the current tech stack and a systems roadmap are useful to have.
Setting AI in Motion: Deploym ent
Requirem ents
W e all have witnessed that ChatG PT  provides evidently wrong answers at
times. An AI might say, “Leonardo da Vinci invented the light bulb.” As
humans, we know this is impossible since there are hundreds of years between
da Vinci’s lifetime and the invention of the light bulb. He simply wasn’t
around to make that discovery.
W hen an AI model makes a mistake, it’s called a hallucination.
We Can’t Afford Hallucination
If an AI tells us that da Vinci invented the light bulb, we can laugh it oﬀ. But
hallucinations can have severe consequences that a business can’t aﬀord. It
becomes a bigger problem when you base your capacity planning on AI
recommendations that lead to an overhire. Or you end up ﬁring people.
e question is: W here are these hallucinations coming from? It has to do
with the training data of the model, whether that’s a text or a mathematical
model. ere’s a common saying in RevOps that goes: “G arbage in, garbage
out.” AI is making the problem exponentially worse. is especially becomes a
problem once we entrust our business data to AI and want to make predictions
and decisions based on that data. High-quality data is essential to prevent
hallucinations.
W hen it comes to data, the problems are not new. I’ve discussed them on
multiple occasions here. is includes duplicate records in the system, storing
the same data points in multiple locations (which creates conﬂicts), custom
data structures that defy logic, and incomplete data ﬁelds like missing job titles
and outdated or inaccurate information. ere is a long list of problems that
are common in many companies. ey all lead to bad decision-making and
lead to even worse AI models.

---

## Page 327

Hallucinations Are Also an Opportunity to
Improve Data Quality
Although hallucinations are a well-known problem due to their incorrect
nature, they also present an opportunity to identify and improve data quality,
making AI models more robust over time. At the same time, we know that AI
boosts productivity. Billions of dollars are ﬂoating into the AI space, and
expectations are high that it can deliver what it promises. I strongly believe it
can. Having worked so long in tech, I see daily how ineﬃcient processes are
and how AI can help.
To make this transition possible, it requires clean data. Only then can AI
deliver insights that are useful.
AIs Impact on Employm ent
“AI will not replace you, but the person using AI w ill.”
– Common saying on the internet.
You may have heard this or a similar statement before. I would argue both
statements are true. AI will clearly replace people; we already see this in First
Line Support Reps. It’s not that one Support Rep uses AI and can do more
than others. Rather, the management team and (probably) the RevOps team
made the decision to deploy a support AI to reduce the people needed to
handle customer support. In this case, AI did replace you.
It’s also true that a person using AI will be more productive than the person
not using it. A Sales Rep that uses AI to automate account research will save 5
to 7 hours of time every week. is time can be spent on selling, which will
make the company more competitive than a company that doesn’t use AI. At
the same time, the market size for the product will not magically increase
overnight, but the company will become more productive in targeting that
market. is means they will need fewer salespeople, and those they do have
will be more productive.

---

## Page 328

RevOps will play a crucial role in deploying AI in businesses, but the
stories should show how these deployments will aﬀect your colleagues’ daily
work and lives. M ost AI projects will lead to redundancies. A responsible
company will make this decision in a tactful and fair manner—at least that
would be the right thing to do.
e thing is, AI deployment is unavoidable at this point. It follows the laws
of business perfectly. Once a few of your competitors start using it, others will
have to follow, or they risk falling behind. e only way to avoid it is to receive
government subsidies (to sustain an otherwise non-proﬁtable business).
Chances are, you’re working in tech, and it’s very unlikely that your
government will subsidize tech jobs as a countermeasure to AI.
Not only are the chances of subsidies low, but they’re also not scalable for
the government. Other sectors would want the same subsidies, and the cost
would be massive. At the same time, there might be governments that actually
subsidize companies to deploy AI to make the country more productive. is
is exactly what China is doing. ey’re investing $1.4 trillion over the coming
six years to further develop AI.45 e U SA announced a similar project, called
Stargate, with plans to invest $500 billion into AI technologies over the
coming years.46
e message is clear. Nothing will stop AI.
The Lean GTM Machine: How AI is
Reshaping RevOps
By Kyle Coleman, CMO at Copy.AI
“Strategic thinking for G T M  operators has undergone a signiﬁcant
transformation over the past few years. Previously, companies focused on
investing heavily in specialized tools, personnel, and manual processes to
drive growth, regardless of cost. is approach was sustainable when capital
was readily available, and investors prioritized top-line growth above all else.
However, the paradigm has shifted dramatically in recent years, with

---

## Page 329

eﬃcient growth becoming the new imperative. is change in expectations
has necessitated a reevaluation of how companies build and optimize their
G T M  engines.
AI has emerged as a game-changing solution to this new challenge, oﬀering
the potential to revolutionize G T M  strategies. Instead of accumulating
disparate investments in point solutions and hyper-specialized staﬀ—a
phenomenon often referred to as “G T M  bloat”—companies can now
leverage AI to identify and eliminate cross-functional friction. is
approach allows organizations to build homegrown applications that
address speciﬁc use cases while ensuring that the resulting processes and
data inform other components of the G T M  system. By doing so, companies
can create a more cohesive and eﬃcient revenue generation ecosystem
without relying on an array of disconnected SaaS solutions.
At the heart of this AI-driven transformation lies the critical role of RevOps.
RevOps stakeholders possess an unparalleled understanding of the systems,
data, tools, and integrations that power the G T M  engine. eir expertise
enables them to orchestrate the seamless integration of Sales, M arketing,
and Customer Success workﬂows, ensuring that AI strategies are
implemented systematically across the entire G T M  process rather than
being siloed within individual departments. is holistic approach
represents the future of revenue operations and highlights the exciting
potential of AI to drive eﬃcient growth in the modern business landscape.”
RevOps as the AI Conductor
W e’ve seen that RevOps is at the center of understanding commercial
operations like no one else in the business. W e know the company strategy,
how it transforms into processes, and which technologies are used to improve
eﬃciency. AI is just another technology, a very powerful one, for that matter.
W e understand better than anyone how revenue engines operate and where
AI needs to be deployed. However, this is only possible if we become experts in
G T M  AI technologies. at’s why the ﬁrst part of the chapter was focused on

---

## Page 330

providing you with a basic understanding of the core AI technologies in
RevOps. W hat follows next is a roadmap to get your business started with it.
e points will be relevant if you have already started with AI or if you are just
at the beginning.
Step 1: Garbage in, Garbage out
In tech, we have the notion of inputs and outputs. You feed in data, the system
processes it, and you get an output. Nearly every information system works on
this basic principle. But here’s the catch: when your input is poor quality (a.k.a
garbage), the output will also be just as bad. G arbage in, garbage out. is
applies to any information technology system, and AI is no exception.
Our goal is to prevent garbage from entering the system. How can we do
that? In earlier chapters, we explored ways to build controls into data captures.
ose are still valid. Pretty much all the principles we discussed in RevOps
before AI was in the picture are still relevant. at’s part of what makes
RevOps such a strong enabler of AI.
Another aspect is automating the inﬂow of data. Here, we typically rely on
three main sources: call recording software, web scraping, intent data, and data
providers.
Call Recording Software
is is an essential piece of software in the times of AI. Not only does it make
note-taking obsolete, which saves the user a lot of time, but it can also update
records automatically in a CRM  or a data warehouse. e underlying speech
recognition and NLP technology analyze all the words and can perform actions
based on that. For example:
•U pdating M ED D IC ﬁelds in the CRM .
•U pdating the close date of a deal.
•D rafting a follow-up email based on the conversation.
•U pdating the next step ﬁeld in the CRM .
•Filtering relevant product feedback.

---

## Page 331

e options for what data we want to extract are endless. But it doesn’t end
here. e calls can be further analyzed to detect patterns, such as whether
certain phrases are more likely to overcome objections, improve deal velocity,
or even close deals faster. e data we gather from call recordings and the
insights we can derive from it are invaluable for any business.
Web Scraping
W eb scraping is the process of extracting publicly available web data using
automated tools. ose tools themselves can be AI or computer programs
without AI. In both cases, the goal is the same: extract relevant data from the
web. You did it so you can:
•U nderstand the marketing campaigns of your competitors.
•Run competitor research (price monitoring, new features, etc.).
•Perform account research (whether companies are hiring, founding
rounds, news, etc.).
•Execute lead generation (ﬁnd phone numbers, contact details, etc.)
•Extract annual reports.
•U nderstand what technologies a company uses.
In short, any publicly available data that is commercially valuable can be
scrapped. W eb scrapers are a hundred times faster than us humans, and they
provide us with a large pool of data we can use for various use cases.
Intent Data and Data Providers
ere are service providers that specialize in selling commercially viable data.
ose data points range from contact data like phone numbers, emails, and job
titles to company data like founding rounds, revenue, employee size, or other
relevant company KP Is. Such service providers can even go into more detail
and provide information about technologies certain companies use, whether
they are hiring or likely to buy services from your company.
is type of data is commonly referred to as intent data because it reﬂects
signals that indicate a potential intention to take action. Intent data and data

---

## Page 332

providers have some similarities to web scraping. ose providers use web
scraping at a large scale to get the data they need but also complement it with
other methods such as screening emails, purchasing lists, and other non-
disclosed methods. W hat matters for a business is that they provide data points
that help you close deals (and feed into your AI).
Keep Your House Clean
If you follow a rigorous approach that includes call recording, web scraping,
and complementing it with purchase intent and contact data, you’ll build a
solid database. To maintain its value, though, it’s crucial to keep that data clean
and up-to-date. Fortunately, all three methods mentioned above support live
updates, which help ensure your systems have the most relevant information.
Periodic data cleanups and ongoing monitoring are also recommended, as
discussed in the Data and Insights chapter.
Step 2: You Need a Hom e for Your Data
You’re probably wondering where all this data will be stored. It’s true that to
have a well-functioning AI model, you need a lot of data. All of this data needs
to be stored somewhere. But where exactly?
First, it’s important to understand what shouldn’t be your primary source of
truth: your CRM . W hile a CRM  is useful for storing certain customer data, it
comes with limitations in terms of format, volume, and speed. at doesn’t
make it unimportant. It just means it’s not designed to handle the demands of
more complex AI use cases.
Instead, you’ll want to focus on three main options: a data warehouse, a
data lakehouse, or a customer data platform.
Data Warehouse
A data warehouse is a centralized system designed to store and manage
structured data for BI, reporting, and analytics. It organizes data in a highly
structured, relational format, making it easy for analysts and business teams to
generate insights using SQL queries. It’s commonly used in Finance,

---

## Page 333

Operations, and traditional BI environments, and it supports historical data
analysis. However, it lacks ﬂexibility for AI/M L workloads or unstructured
data processing.
Data Lakehouse
A data lakehouse merges the beneﬁts of a data warehouse and a data lake
(which supports both raw and structured data), enabling both structured and
unstructured data storage. It supports advanced analytics, machine learning,
and real-time processing while maintaining the governance and performance of
a traditional warehouse. is hybrid approach is ideal for AI-driven businesses,
as it allows for seamless data integration, scalable storage, and fast processing
for complex workloads like image recognition, NLP, and predictive modeling.
Custom er Data Platform  (CDP)
A CD P is a specialized system designed to collect, unify, and activate customer
data across multiple channels for personalized marketing and customer
engagement. U nlike data warehouses or lakehouses, which store diverse
enterprise data, a CD P focuses solely on customer interactions, behaviors, and
preferences. It enables real-time customer segmentation, AI-driven
recommendations, and predictive analytics, which make it a valuable tool for
M arketing, Sales, and Customer Success teams.
e table below compares all three options side-by-side and rates them for
their AI use case.

---

## Page 334

W hich one you need will depend on the stage of your company. If you
work in a large enterprise, such as a Fortune 500 company, then you’ll typically
have all three: a data warehouse supports structured reporting and business
intelligence, a data lakehouse enables AI/M L at scale with structured and
unstructured data, and the CD P optimizes customer data for marketing,
personalization, and engagement. Of course, this is very costly and only
recommended for large enterprises.

---

## Page 335

As a mid-size company, you would likely only end up using two of them:
•D ata W arehouse + CDP if you focus on analytics and customer
personalization.
•D ata Lakehouse + CDP if you prioritize AI-driven personalization and
real-time analytics.
e latter would be recommended for AI use cases that are recommended
in this chapter.
For small companies or startups, AI use cases often focus on one primary
data strategy. For example, an AI startup building a chatbot might use a data
lakehouse to process large volumes of text data, train NLP models, and
improve real-time responses. Similarly, an IoT  company developing smart
home devices could use a data lakehouse to analyze sensor data from thousands
of devices in order to detect anomalies and optimize energy consumption.
W hereas an e-commerce startup selling fashion items might use a CD P to
track customer behavior, personalize product recommendations, and automate
targeted email campaigns, and a subscription-based ﬁtness app could use the
same approach by collecting user workout history and preferences to deliver
AI-driven exercise suggestions and retention-focused push notiﬁcations.
Lastly, a data warehouse would have fewer AI use cases. A FinTech startup
that oﬀers small business loans stores transactional data in a data warehouse for
ﬁnancial reporting, risk analysis, and compliance audits. An AI use case could
involve using machine learning models within the warehouse to detect
fraudulent transactions by analyzing spending patterns and ﬂagging anomalies
in real-time.
AI Agents Start with Call Recordings
By Anis Bennaceur, CEO of Attention.com
AI agents that leverage both call and email data can be a far more
trustworthy source of truth than a CRM  alone.

---

## Page 336

Rather than relying on manually typed notes or biased updates, these agents
examine real conversations, detecting subtle cues like competitor mentions,
buying signals, or product feedback. By handling hours’ worth of calls and
inbox activity in minutes, they perform tasks that otherwise would take
days or weeks of human labor. From auto-completing opportunity stages to
fully updating knowledge bases, AI agents transform raw communication
data into usable insights that drive everything from qualiﬁcation to
forecasting.
Below is a list of the kinds of AI agents that may be extracted from call
recordings and emails, categorized by type:
Enablem ent:
•Knowledge Base Builder: Captures FAQs, best practices, and objection
handling scenarios from real conversations and synchronizes them to
wikis or FAQs in real time.
•Competitive Intel/Rep Intelligence: Detects competing product mentions
and trends on calls and emails and oﬀers real-time competitive insights to
the team.
•Role Play AI: Simulate call scenarios to provide real-time coaching or
training modules on real customer conversations.
Business D evelopm ent:
•AI Inbound BD Rs: Can qualify leads on a call based on the methodology
and knowledge base of your choice and generate the action items from
the conversations.
•Qualiﬁcation Alerts: Automatically compares call and email content to
ICP or M ED D IC/BANT  standards and prompts reps to escalate or book
meetings.
Account Executives:

---

## Page 337

•Call Prep Agent: Reviews past conversations and emails ahead of a
meeting and preps a rep before their meeting.
•Pipeline Analyzer: Reviews transcripts for stalled deals, hidden objections,
or looming risks.
•Action Items Reminder: Identiﬁes tasks like submitting quotes or
planning demos and automatically generates reminders in calendars or
task managers.
RevOps:
•NPS/Customer Health Detection: Monitors sentiment and keywords on
support calls and email discussions, updating health scores or signaling
churn risk.
•AI M anager/AI Ops: Oversees system integrations and data management
and ensures the seamless handoﬀ of insights across departments.
Cross-Functional Collaboration:
•Onboarding/Training Agents: Trains new hires with real call and email
examples, oﬀering guided lessons tailored to speciﬁc scenarios.
•Internal Comms/Alerts: Publishes product feedback or price problems
discovered from calls to product, ﬁnance, or marketing departments—
shortening the feedback cycle.
… and so much more!
All these agents replace full-time employees, automate end-to-end
functions, and allow for leaner teams to be better at execution.
By translating all interactions into structured, actionable data, AI agents
remove CRM -only approaches’ blind spots and allow teams to focus on
higher-value work. is union of call and email data tied to a system of

---

## Page 338

record oﬀers unparalleled visibility and productivity—turning tedious
conversations into a powerful driver of revenue growth.
Step 3: Let’s Get Started with AI
Congrats, you have data, and it’s properly stored. Now, you can make use of it!
e use cases of AI in G T M  and RevOps are endless. I could write a whole
book about the subject, and others are doing likewise. As the topic goes
beyond the scope of the book, I just want to group the main use cases in the
table below.

---

## Page 339

e ﬁrst category of AI Agents and Autonomous Systems is the most
promising one, as those autonomous agents will be able to make decisions on
their own and thereby have the potential to do the job of a human (E.g.,
replacing a SD R or a service agent). At the time of writing in April 2025, those
agents are promising but not mature enough to fully replace a human. But I
believe it’s only a question of time until they are fully operational (like I
illustrated in the Umbrella AI Corp. example).

---

## Page 340

W hat’s more promising are AI W orkﬂows, the objectives of which are to
mainly replace repetitive workﬂows. ink in terms of doing account research,
competitive monitoring, or enriching records. ose AI-enhanced workﬂows
are already widespread and will multiply even further. M any automation and
no-code tools like n8n, Zapier, or M ake® make those workﬂows easy to
establish.
One of the most powerful use cases is AI-driven analytics. W hen a data
lake or CD P is ﬁlled with rich, high-volume data, it becomes a strong
foundation for advanced analysis. AI can deliver highly accurate insights into
customer purchasing behavior, attribution models, and churn predictions—
often much faster than traditional human analysis.
Pro T ip: Request an AI experimental budget. U se this budget to experiment w ith
various use cases. e technology is developing very quickly, so you probably don’t
want to go all-in with the ﬁrst one available. Instead, test a few, learn from the
results, and maintain ﬂexibility as you reﬁne your strategy.
Closely related to analytics is the opportunity to greatly improve both
internal and external customer experiences. You can use the data points to
build the most personalized marketing campaigns by showing exactly what a
customer wants to see at the right time. On the internal side, you can have the
next generation of enablement: AI training tailored to the speciﬁc learning
needs of each employee. Imagine, everyone has their own personal expert
coach!
Lastly, AI will strongly inﬂuence G T M  and RevOps strategy. At a
minimum, it will become a committee member and help make important
decisions around sales strategy, territory design, or commission planning.
As these roles start to blend, things get even more interesting. Picture an AI
agent working alongside a Chief Revenue Oﬃcer, a VP of RevOps, or a Head
of M arketing—handling tasks, crunching numbers, and oﬀering smart
suggestions. If AI really lives up to its potential, there might not be much left
for us humans to do in those areas. at kind of shift comes with big societal

---

## Page 341

and ethical questions, which are outside the scope of this book and better left
to the experts. Of course, there’s also a chance AI never gets that powerful.
Time will tell. W hat’s clear right now is that AI is already changing the game,
and it’s only going to keep transforming how companies work.
You, dear reader who works in RevOps, are in the best position to be in the
driving seat of this change!
Let’s build the company of the future!
Socratic Reﬂections
AI is changing RevOps for good. Let’s turn to some Socrates questions:
•D o you have an AI strategy for GT M  and RevOps in your business? If
not, what should it include?
•W hat area in your company would beneﬁt most from AI? Can you ﬁnd a
trial use case?
•D oes your company work with sensible data, or is it may be impacted by
AI regulation? Reﬂecting on that can impact your vendor decision.
•How can you ensure that you respect the garbage in, garbage out
principle to avoid hallucinations?
•W hat potential do you have for web scraping, call recording, intent and
customer data?
•W here should you store all your data? Have you talked to IT  to develop
the best AI storage for your data?
•W hat AI workﬂow can you implement this quarter? W hat are the quick
wins?

---

## Page 342

CHAPTER 11
THE FINAL EQU ILIBRIU M –
REVOPS IN FU LL MOTION
W hen deployed correctly, RevOps is magic. You’ll experience never-before-seen
growth, your Revenue teams will run smoothly, and you will satisfy your
customers. W hat appears like magic is a scientiﬁc approach to growing a
business. Proven frameworks, methodologies, and processes help you reach
your goal. at’s the RevOps Pendulum.
Just like Newton’s Pendulum relies on perfect alignment to keep moving,
the RevOps Pendulum only works when teams are in sync. W ithout
alignment, departments stay siloed and disconnected. RevOps helps break
down those silos, aligning teams so the company can operate as a uniﬁed force
for growth.
Figure 11.1 RevOps alignm ent in the Pendulum

---

## Page 343

In the book, I’ve stressed the importance of alignment. is is really at the
core of what RevOps is. To make that happen, strong communication and
persuasion skills are essential. In fact, I’d even go so far as to say that your soft
skills are even more important than your hard skills. Invest in those, and you’ll
be unstoppable!
On multiple occasions, I highlighted the importance of data quality. Your
decision-making depends on clean data, which is why it’s one of the core pillars
of RevOps. But more importantly, if we look at the future of AI-driven
businesses, then data becomes even more important. D o yourself and your
business a favor and prioritize data.
Lastly, AI is the real game-changer for both G T M  and RevOps. W hen I
started writing this book, I thought it would focus solely on RevOps—a
discipline I care deeply about. But the breakthrough of AI completely reshaped
not just RevOps but the entire business landscape. at’s why AI has become
such a central theme in this book.
W hat I’ve shared with you about RevOps still matters. It’s the foundation.
But that foundation alone won’t be enough going forward. To stay relevant,
you need to become an expert in AI. at’s why, as I wrote this book, I dove
deeper into AI myself and included those insights here—to help you grow into
the kind of RevOps leader the future demands.
e best part? RevOps is uniquely positioned to drive AI transformation
within companies. So lean in and be a part of it!
Finally, I’ll conclude this book with practical advice on how you can prove
the value of RevOps and its future.
Proving RevOps’ Value
I often hear that A) leadership does not see the value of RevOps or B) RevOps
professionals have a hard time showing its value.
Here’s the thing… if you apply the strategies and frameworks outlined in
this book, you will deliver massive value to the business. I’m talking about an
impact so signiﬁcant that it might seem almost absurd—so much so that your

---

## Page 344

company could end up wondering how to invest all the extra revenue you’re
helping generate.
And no, I’m not exaggerating—I’m making a point. at point is this: it all
starts with you truly believing, with every ﬁber of your being, that RevOps can
create that level of value.
Are you with me?
G reat! Here are seven practical tips on how to show this value to your
stakeholders.
Speak the Language of Leadership
RevOps: “I built this new automation using API calls and web scraping while at
the same time checking for duplicates and enriching our records while also scoring
them. Do you want to see the workﬂow?”
CEO: “W hat are you talking about? Does it make us more revenue?”
Conversations like this are happening in many companies all over the
world. RevOps presents a very technical solution to an audience that does not
share the technical language they use. is is a missed opportunity. For
RevOps, it’s crucial to speak the language of leadership to drive business
impact. e technical details don’t matter at the leadership level. Leadership is
concerned about:
•How many bookings will it create?
•How many new qualiﬁed leads will it generate?
•How much pipeline will be generated?
•How does it improve the win rate?
•Has it had an impact on ARR, TCV, CLT V, etc?
Leaders are busy; they need to make sure that the business is running. ey
want to beat the competition, meet investors’ expectations, and keep growing.
Let’s try the above conversation again.

---

## Page 345

RevOps: “Let me introduce you to Project “M oney Printer.” W ith new AI
workﬂows, we will increase our qualiﬁed leads by 40%. W e already saw that in the
ﬁrst month when we increased the pipeline by 50%, along with our win rate by
15%, due to the better quality of leads. In total, we see a revenue increase of
$60,000 in the ﬁrst month.”
CRO: “Project “M oney Printer” lives up to its name. W hat can I do to make it
more successful?”
Fram e RevOps as a business driver, not a
support function.
Above, I asked you to think of RevOps as this insane value-generating business
function. It is that, but you also have to frame it as such.
It has to become your identity.
If you believe RevOps is just about admin, then your identity will become
that of an admin. If you believe RevOps is just automation, then your identity
will become that of a G T M  engineer. If you believe RevOps is a business
driver, then your identity will become that of a business driver.
You will radiate to others what you are. You are what you think you are.
ink of yourself as a business driver, and you will become it if you walk the
talk.
Be proactive with value-driving projects
If you believe RevOps is a powerful business driver, and you come up with
incredible ideas—but they never leave your head—then nothing actually
changes. I call that La La Land. Everything is amazing in La La Land, but La
La Land is just ﬁction.
You need to be proactive in working out projects that drive the business
forward. ose projects must then be tied to the language the leadership team
speaks.

---

## Page 346

AI is a great opportunity here. It’s changing the business landscape, and
you can be the change-maker in your business. If you don’t have an AI budget
yet, request an experimental one. Link the request to business objectives. It
should be certain that you will get it. en, show quick wins with AI and start
with a focus on workﬂows.
Becom e an Expert in AI
is one should go without saying, but I will highlight it one more time.
Become the AI expert on your Revenue team. You don’t need to become an AI
Engineer, but you do need to develop an understanding of how to use AI tools
to generate business value for your company. e good news is that you already
understand the commercial operations like no one else. Now, you just need to
deploy AI to make it even more eﬃcient, proﬁtable, and cost-eﬃcient.
Always Link Your Projects to OKRs
A practical tip to deliver value is to link your projects to OK Rs. If your
business doesn’t have OKR s, then link them to the strategy or your core KP Is.
For example, you’re not working on a churn prediction model just because
someone asked you to; you’re doing it because it ties directly to an OKR
focused on reducing churn. It’s a highly strategic project, even if it’s technical
in nature. W hat really matters is the outcome, not the method. People care far
more about what you achieve than how you get there. Never forget that.
A very practical step is to become a co-owner of the OKR s. For example,
your VP of Customer Success might own the OKR  to reduce churn by 4% by
Q4. RevOps contributes to that goal by implementing an AI-driven churn
prediction model.
Pace Projects Right. It’s a Marathon, Not a
Sprint

---

## Page 347

In RevOps, we tend to get too excited about new projects. W e want to
implement an AI forecast and a new sales playbook and create a new churn
prediction model while implementing a new CRM . If you see yourself in this,
then you have to slow down. You might think that you deliver a lot of value to
your stakeholders, but what you are doing is scaring them oﬀ. Change takes
time. People need time to adjust to new things. Change is even scary to some.
Always keep that in mind. It’s better to deliver one or two strong projects that
get fully implemented than to work on four or six that never really go
anywhere.
Be Vocal About Your Worth
OKR s, proactivity, and having an identity as a business driver all show that
RevOps brings value to the business.
You really need to vocalize it.
is means to insist on praise when it’s earned. You don’t need to shout
about your wins, but you should conﬁdently share the impact you’ve made.
at could mean taking more ownership, mentioning your results in strategy
calls, or casually updating leaders on your work over lunch. If you’re in a
hybrid role, make sure to show up at the oﬃce. If you’re fully remote, ﬁnd
ways to meet with leadership in person—you’ll regret it if you don’t.
is also means you should praise others when they do great work—
whether it’s someone on your team who developed a powerful integration, a
Sales Rep who gave you insights from the ﬁeld that improved the process, or
the VP of M arketing who challenged your thinking which resulted in a better
idea. Earn your praise, and give praise when others earn it.
Know W hen to Leave
W hen you put all of this into practice, you can become a truly strategic
RevOps, if you’re in the right environment. at said, even with everything
done right, there are still factors that can work against you. ose are:

---

## Page 348

•Leadership doesn’t want to understand RevOps despite your best eﬀorts.
•Leadership does not give the necessary resources to RevOps.
•You are in a dying industry. (e best RevOps engine can’t save you
here.)
•Your boss and stakeholders take all the credit.
•You get pushed only to do administrative work.
•ere’s a siloed culture beyond repair.
•e business is too small for RevOps, and its value can’t be proven.
If you see two or more of these characteristics in your company, it may be
time to move on. Even your best eﬀorts can only go so far in the wrong
environment. It’s important to understand that the problem isn’t you in that
scenario. You might choose to give it six to twelve months to see if things
improve, but if nothing changes despite your hard work, it’s best to leave and
not look back. You deserve a better future.
The Coming Shift – W hat’s Next for RevOps
I see a bright future for RevOps. I see a Pendulum that never stops moving!
e sky really is the limit. Here are three key shifts shaping its future.
Shift # 1: Rise of RevOps Outside of the
Technology Sector
e potential of RevOps goes far beyond SaaS. As we have seen in the Finance
chapter, many businesses now include a recurring revenue component like real
estate, consulting, newspapers, insurance, or advertising. M ore industries are
becoming SaaS-iﬁed. ere are now Food-as-a-Service, Bikes-as-a-Service, or
even Lights-as-a-Service. ey all have a recurring revenue model and can
beneﬁt hugely from RevOps.
Having said that, even businesses without a recurring revenue model can
greatly beneﬁt from a RevOps strategy. e alignment between M arketing and

---

## Page 349

Sales alone is worth it.
Besides, which businesses don’t want to sell more of the same products to
the same customers?
Trend # 2: RevOps as a Strategic Business
Partner
e one key takeaway from this book is that RevOps is a strategic business
function. A RevOps leader should understand every part of the revenue in
your business. is goes from M arketing to Sales to Customer Success, but it
can also expand to Legal, Finance, and Product. Chances are, nobody else in
your business will have such a bird’s-eye view on your business.
D o you know what we call such people? CEO-material.
Steve Jobs was the visionary who made the Apple brand big. Tim Cook was
the operator who scaled the business to its current heights. RevOps is a factory
for operators that deliver recurring revenue.
Shift # 3: RevOps Facilitates Leaner
Companies in the Future Through AI
e company of the future will be leaner. ere will be less need for people in
various functions, especially Revenue teams. AI will be a powerful change.
RevOps will be in the driving seat of the evolution. It’s a unique
opportunity to apply all of RevOps’ business knowledge to this powerful
technology.
e RevOps Pendulum only gets more accelerated with AI.
Be part of that future.
The end
